# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kafka Streams topology build chain in apache/kafka. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Topology Build Chain Summary

I've created a comprehensive `answer.json` file documenting the complete chain from logical topology to physical execution:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Entry Point**: `StreamsBuilder.build()` - User-facing method that initiates topology compilation

2. **DSL Optimization**: `InternalStreamsBuilder.buildAndOptimizeTopology()` - Applies graph transformations and optimizations to the logical topology

3. **State Store Registration**: `StateStoreNode.writeToTopology()` - Registers state stores with the topology builder via `addStateStore()`

4. **Logical→Physical Compilation**: `InternalTopologyBuilder.buildTopology()` - Converts the logical DSL graph to a physical ProcessorTopology

5. **ProcessorNode Construction**: `InternalTopologyBuilder.build()` - Creates the actual ProcessorNode graph with proper wiring of state stores

6. **Physical Representation**: `ProcessorTopology` - Contains ProcessorNodes, SourceNodes, SinkNodes, and their connectivity

7. **Task Initialization**: `StreamTask.initializeTopology()` - Initializes processor nodes during task startup

8. **Processor Initialization**: `ProcessorNode.init()` - Initializes individual processors with context and state stores

9. **Store Management**: `StoreBuilder` and `StoreFactory` - Abstractions for state store creation and management

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains all files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining the complete topology building chain with file paths and line numbers for reference.

localStore.get(key);\\n448:      * }</pre>\\n449:      * Note that {@link GlobalKTable} always applies {@code \\\"auto.offset.reset\\\"} strategy {@code \\\"earliest\\\"}\\n450:      * regardless of {@link GlobalKTable} for the specified topic\\n458:      */\\n459:     public synchronized <K, V> GlobalKTable<K, V> globalTable(final String topic,\\n460:                                                               final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\\n461:                                                               final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\\n462: import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * {@code StreamsBuilder} provides the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n51:  *\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * It is a This also means that the work\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n190:      * <p>\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n194:      *\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n197:      */\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     /**\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n204:      * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n206:      * <p>\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics.
